And another thing to know about the instruments of moving teeth are similar and akin to the other instruments.
But the wise and subtle artisans in the art find for themselves many ways according to what they understand of the operation and the diverse illnesses; for there are diverse illnesses which the ancients did not name or put into proper instruments by their forms of diverse species.
But if the bone of the jaw or of the other bones of the mouth is cracked, then it must be cured on that in its place with what is convenient to him of the instruments and forceps which we have said in the extraction of the roots of the teeth, and aid yourself by the gesture of which this is the shape:
And there must be some thickness in it little by little, and it must be bound or held by the mouth so that it does not escape or leak until all of the bone is forgotten; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines to that.
But if there is a small breaking in the bone, then scrape that of that breaking and of its blackness, and cure it within until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of teeth which are prominent above the others.
When teeth are prominent not according to their natural form by those the shape is lacking, and especially when it happens in women, and especially in elderly women; therefore you must consider: if the tooth is next to another tooth, and it is not possible for there to be a lancing or lining of it, then remove that one; but if it is not attached to another tooth, then you insert that one with this instrument of which this is the shape; and it is similar to pig's tooth, and it must be made of Indian iron with an extremely sharp end.
And your incision should be such that you insert it into the tooth in several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and not cut another of the teeth.
And if it is a prominent tooth exposed to grinding, then you grind that one with an Indian iron file of which this is the shape:
And let it all be of Indian iron and the margin evenly; and let it have small points like a file with which needles are made, and with which the tooth is ground little by little in several days with facility, so that no other tooth is cut or broken. And then you line it at its end, and scrape it with a sharp razor.
And if it is a tooth of which one part is cracked and cuts the tongue, then you must grind it within until the sharp edge of that fracture is worn down and flattened so that the tongue is not cut nor speech impaired.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the restoration of broken teeth with gold or silver wire.
When it happens to the teeth that there is concussion and removal by striking or falling, and the patient cannot hold onto what they chew, and you have cured them with astringent medicines, and your cure has not helped, then so that they do not rot, it is useful that they are bound with gold wire and not silver, for silver becomes black and soon rots after several days, but gold does not change at all.
And let the wire be of such thinness and thickness according to the quantity that can enter between the teeth; and the shape of the binding is that you take the wire and place twice its length between two healthy teeth, and then let it grow with two tortuosities of the wire between two broken ones, or if one or more, within so that the thread comes to the healthy tooth from the other part. And then repeat the binding within to the part from which you began, and strengthen your hand with facility and skill within so that it is not broken.
And let your binding be such that you bind the wire over the roots of the teeth so that it does not leak.
And then you insert the wire’s excess ends with forceps or tweezers, and draw those to each other in every place with gestures, and convert them and hide them between the healthy tooth and the broken one, so that it does not harm the tongue. And then let her tightly close it thus with Roman wax.
But if it is loose or broken, strengthen that or those with another wire in the same way at all times.
And this is the form of teeth and the figure of the binding of two healthy teeth and two broken ones, thus with their threads bound:
And when it happens that one tooth or two return to their places of origin, and they are regrown thus as we have recommended, and that they rot again.
And it does not do anything but good artisans and the wise.
And sometimes it is apt for some cause of the bones of a cow, and it is made in the shape of teeth, and placed in the place where the tooth fails, and is strengthened as we have said, and remains and serves with him for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the incision of the thread which appears in the tongue and it prohibits speech.
This ligament which appears under the tongue some times, or is natural to him, or it happens accidentally and occurs because of a wound that is already consolidated.
And the operation on it is that you open the mouth of the patient, the jaw being held in your hand; and elevate the tongue, and then insert the nervous thread according to its length so that the tongue is released from its binding.
But if there is any hardness or knottiness in it, and that is standing because of consolidation of the wound, then you cut a notch and split it according to its length so that you have split the thread and the knot is dissolved.
And beware that there is not made a fissure in the lip of meat, and you split here the artery and blood flows out.
And then it is washed with vinegar or wine or vinegar and water, and then the patient spits out; so that the tongue be not bound up by another wound.
But if blood flows out, place on the spot vinegar triphled; but if blood vents, then cauterize the spot with a burning cautery appropriate to that. And then it is cured by the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the extraction of ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes it happens under the tongue an apostema resembling a small nut which prohibits speech, and strong is enlarged within so that it fills the mouth.
And the operation on it is that you open the mouth of the patient facing the sun and consider the apostema.
And if you see it of a dusky or black color, hard, to which the patient does not respond with feeling, then do not touch that because it is rotten.
And if it is turned white and humid, then you put the ointment on it, and insert that subtle sponge, and insert the whole thing; and if blood comes out during your operation, then you stop above with a trussed bandage, so that the blood is restricted.
Then return to your work while it is still wet with the ointment, and wash it with sweet wine and salt; and heal it with another healing until it is healed.
Chapter 36.
Of the extraction of an abscess from both ears, and of that which is in the throat, and of other abscesses.
When an abscess appears in the throat, it is like glands which are clustered together, which are cut open and are called both ears, which when you treat them with what we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then you should consider whether the abscess is hard, of a dusky color, with little feeling; then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of a red color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron for fear of bleeding; unless you let that one remain until it is ripe, and either you will cut it out or it will burst on its own.
And if it is of a white color, soft, and the root of it is fine, then that one should be cut into.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, whether the abscess has rested completely or has diminished by any diminution; and then have the patient lie down facing the sun, and his head be in your lap, and open the mouth of him, and the servant holding his hands press the tongue of him downward with a noble instrument, of which this is the shape:
And it should be made of silver or bronze, and be fine like a needle.
And when you press with that the tongue and it is shown to you the abscess, and you put over that your thumb, then take ointment and insert that into the hollow, and draw that out to the outside parts as much as you can. Another way is that you draw some cause from the membranes; then insert that with an instrument of which this is the shape:
Another way is that you draw some cause from the membranes; then insert that with an instrument of which this is the shape: It is like a pair of forceps, except that its ends are bent so that the aperture of each of those is in the direction of the other, very sharp, and it should be made of iron coated in wax.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then insert that with a sponge of which this is the shape: and it should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other side.
And after you have inserted one hole, insert the other according to this method of insertion, and then let the patient gargle with water.
But if blood comes out, then gargle with water of cooking liquid from the rind of pomegranate or leaf of myrtle, and similar to that of the causes of constriction so that the flow of blood is restricted, and then heal that until it is healed.
And sometimes in the throat there are other abscesses besides those two ears; and insert those according to what has been said about the insertion of two holes equally.
And I have once treated a woman of an abscess which was in her throat, and that abscess had turned dusky in color, with little feeling; it had closed up her throat, and the woman could breathe only through a narrow opening, and she had prohibited herself from eating and drinking water, and she was on the verge of death if she had not taken any food or drink for one or two days.
And that abscess had pushed so much that it had made two bumps within which fluid would drip through two openings.
So I cut her throat with a scalpel and put in one of them the ointment, and drew that out, and it came out from her a great portion; then I cut into where I understood was the other opening, and then I closed her mouth, pressed her tongue, and then I put the ointment on that abscess.
And then I cut off a great portion of it, and only a little blood flowed from it. So absolutely her throat was closed, and she began to drink water at once, and then took food; therefore I did not cease cutting that abscess many times for a long time, and the abscess returned in the place of it, which cut into it again and again as long as it was prolonged.
So I had iron and cauterized her throat, therefore she was in great distress; and then I walked around and did not know what God had done to that; therefore I believed.
Chapter 37.
Of the incision of a hernia when it is abscessed.
When pus comes out of the hernia and it is abscessed and long, then that is called a perpendicular hernia; and if it is swollen and round at the bottom, then it is called a buba.
But when it is healed with what has been said in the division and does not conform to your cure, and the abscess cauterized is already old and thin, then you should insert that which is swelled around and round; and if it is long and blood comes out of it, dusky or black in color, and there is no feeling in it, then beware of cutting into it, for fear over the patient.
And when you see that according to the manner that I have said of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient lie down and press his tongue with an instrument of which you process its shape, then put ointment in the new one, and draw that out from above and insert it with one of the two instruments which I said about the insertion of two holes.
And beware that you do not insert that unless it is drawn up over the natural term by addition, for if you cut into it more, you will draw out its speech.
And then after the incision, use that which we have recommended in the insertion of two holes, and heal that until it is healed.
But if the patient is frightened by the incision of it, then use the iron in cauterizing it without fear, and the manner of cauterizing in it is not but with sharp water; and let the patient's head be in your lap, and then press his tongue with the instrument which we have said, and then take that water which we said in the chapter on cauterization, and conform to living cause, and put that not thick nor thin, and of that fill the hollow of the instrument of which this is the shape:
Let the end of it be hollow in which the medicine is paused as with the concavity of a spoon; and put the instrument over the hernia, and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva or spittle drips from the mouth of him due to the intrinsic medicine, so that nothing goes down into the throat of him and let it drip.
And then hold your hand over the medicine, and express that onto the uvula for a space of half an hour until you see it blackened and soothed by the biting of the medicine.
And if you want, take a cloth and wrap that over the end of the iron, and immerse the iron in the medicine, and insert the end into a tube of wax so that the iron adheres to that tube; and do that as many times until you accomplish what you want from cauterizing the grape, then let it dry and fall off after three or four days.
And if you feel that the medicine needs to be repeated, repeat it, and then cauterize the area around the ulcer with a cotton swab dipped in wine, and cleanse the area around the ulcer with the water from the medicine, and wash it with rubbing alcohol, and treat the inside of the ulcer with ointments until it heals.
And this type of treatment is more safe than surgery and less painful and terrifying.
Sometimes the ulcer is healed with a liquid that is thinner than cauterization and incision, for it is healed by sublimation in this way: take calamine, hyssop, oregano, rue, Arabic scordium, camomile, bruised plants and similar to these herbs, and put all those causes, or some of them, in a vessel, and let them be steeped in mild wine; and the vessel should be warm with decent heat, and there should be a hole in the middle of the vessel, on which an appropriate hollow instrument made of silver or bronze is placed; it should be made of silver or bronze.
And the end of this instrument is inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the steam reaches the ulcer on the glottis, until the ulcer is very foggy.
And then repeat this several times until it is dry, and beware of performing this treatment at the beginning of an inflammation of an ulcer, for it would make the inflammation worse; rather, you should wait for the declaration of the ulcer's cautery.
But if you do not have this instrument, then take a cane and attach a piece of holly at its end, so that the mouth of the patient is protected, for the holly's close prevents the steam from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter 38.
On the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat, and of other causes.
Sometimes there is adhesion in the throat or a thorn in the foot or some other cause.
Then you should extract what is visible from these, by looking at it with an instrument in front of the sun, so that you can see what is in the throat.
And what is hidden and concealed in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food has digested in the stomach, for often the cause of the throat lies hidden by vomiting; or let the patient swallow a piece of napkin or a leaf of lettuce or a piece of dry bread; or let him swallow a piece of dried sponge, and then apply vinegar to it strongly, and then let the patient swallow it, for when it reaches the place where the thorns are, they will be dislodged. And if you take an eel and apply vinegar to it, and let it be inside and applied, it will be extracted; or take a needle and push it in and push it out.
But if they are not dislodged by those causes which we have mentioned, then use an instrument made of lead according to this form:
And it should be thicker than a small needle, and at its end there should be a hollow which you can insert into the patient's throat easily.
And let the patient' head be elevated, and beware of touching his bones in the throat, so that he does not cough or vomit, or that the doctor holds his hand over his mouth.
But if the patient himself inserts it, because of his knowledge of the location of the cause and pulls the instrument upwards, all this according to the amount for which he is prepared until it is dislodged.
Chapter 39.
On the extraction of blood-letting annexed to the throat.
When blood-letting has been administered with what we have said in the division of treatment by medicines, and it does not help, then consider the throat of the patient towards the sun, for you should have applied his tongue with an instrument which we have recommended.
Therefore if you see blood, extract it gently with a small needle or with decently thin tweezers.
And if you are unable to extract it, then take a hollow tube and insert it into the throat of the patient, and then place a hot iron in the hollow of the tube, and do this as many times as necessary (until the blood-letting is stopped and it ceases from the throat), and let the patient abstain from water all day.
And then take a sponge saturated with rubbing alcohol, and open the patient's mouth with it, and wash his mouth with it; and do not let any cause enter into his throat, and do not let him drink anything for an hour or more with his hand, for the blood-letting will soon cease when he drinks.
But if it is not stopped by what we have recommended, then subliminate the throat with camphor or asafetida using the instrument which we have recommended for sublimination of the ulcer.
Do this, so that in whatever way it falls.
And there is another way of operating in sublimination of it: take a vessel in which are burning coals and the vessel should be covered with a cover on top of which there is a hole, and the end of the instrument should be placed in that hole; then apply the sublimation; and let the patient open his mouth over the end of the tube, and close his mouth so that the sublimation is not wasted until you know that the sublimation has reached the blood-letting, for the blood-letting will soon cease.
And if it does not cease, then repeat the sublimation several times, and let the patient abstain from drinking, and eat salt and alder wood, and do not drink water, and so by this regimen it will be stopped.
And this is the form of the instrument with which blood-letting from the throat is extracted when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps except for having some curvature: which is applied to the throat, and its end is similar to a wooden beak of a stork, which is smooth, in which there is a cut with lime, so that when it grasps something, it does not slip.
Chapter 40.
In which is the sum of the tongue in perception of ulcers and in section of them.
Ulcers are of various kinds, from various causes, according to which we remember them, each in this book.
And they are diverse in penetration and section of them by two ways: one is by the nature of ulcers themselves; and by what we perceive from humidity.
And the second way is by the places in which they occur, for the accidental ulcer on the head is different from the accidental ulcer on the heel; and the ulcer in a fleshy place is different from the ulcer in a joint; and each of them has its own treatment by operation.
And there are also some ulcers which do not need to be penetrated, but rather require maturation of the pus in them or completion of them.
And there are other ulcers which are not cut but rather have成熟(maturation) of the pus in them or completion of them. And there are also some ulcers which are near joints, for when there is an ulcer on a joint, its matter is prolonged to the parts around it, and very often the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, for this is the cause of contraction of that member; or it is near a main member, and if you delay penetration of it until it becomes mature, it will corrupt the main member; or it is near the anus, so penetrate it when it is not mature; and do not cut into a crux, unless there is complete digestion, but rather that which is near the anus, so that it does not corrupt the front of it and is prolonged to the parts around it, and there has been made a fistula, or that which is at the end of it and has not healed. You should know when to pierce the pustule, and that time is when it has matured.
You should know that it has matured when there is a decrease in pain and fever, as well as a decrease in redness and pulsation, and the head of the pustule becomes pointed, along with other signs.
You should also know that piercing should be done in the lowest part of the pustule and where pus is coming from the healing of the eminence.
And piercing should always be done through the length of the skin or body, if the pustules are on the hands or feet, and in the places of the veins, nerves, and arteries; and in all places alike where there is no reflection; for in those where there is a reflection, use piercing according to that member.
But when the pustule is in a fleshy place, it is better to pierce it after digestion has been confirmed according to what we have said; for if you pierce it before that, the body of the pus and dirt are prolonged, as well as the lips of it being hardened and its depth.
But some pustules are pierced according to the width of the skin or body due to necessity, or according to that of which the member is in need.
And you should administer a small piercing for small pustules, a large and ample piercing for large pustules, or many piercings according to the diversity of the size of the pustules.
And there are others of pustules in which the membrane is hollowed out and cut, when it is done so that bread is made, as it happens with those on the scrotum and testicles.
And there are those that are cut with a section having three angles; and there is one that is cut in the shape of a leaf of bay laurel, as are the pustules on the elbows.
And there are those in which round and lunar sections are administered, and similar to those.
But that which is not tipped as are superficial pustules, you should pierce it with a superficial piercing, or simply a flat one.
And when the pustule is large and has collected a lot of pus, you should pierce it and not be afraid to extract all the pus at that time; having extracted a part of it, then plug the pustule again on the next day, then extract a larger portion, and do this repeatedly until it is completely drained.
And especially if the patient is of a cold nature, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an old person in decline; for the animal spirit is often resolved by the discharge of pus, and it rarely harms them, and you should operate on them.
Therefore take great care with this chapter, and when you pierce these pustules, cleanse the wounds and consider if the wound of the pustule is small or a flat section, then you should administer the cauterizations of old wine or vinegar; but if the pustule is large and the fissures of the piercing are many, then you should place a plug in each crack as they appear.
And if a part of the membrane is torn off or you have hollowed it out in the circuit, then you should complete it with old wine or a thread made of linen cloth, just as when you treat wounds or roots, without moisture; and strengthen it on the third day; and then process and cure it as you would any other wound.
But if bleeding occurs at the time of your operation, then you should administer water mixed with vinegar and wine in which a linen cloth has been soaked, and place it over the site of the bleeding many times.
But if the bleeding persists, then you should administer regimens and curettages, and powders which I have recommended in other places of this book.
But if it is in the winter time, and the site of the pustule is a place of many nerves, then you should soak cotton in wine and oil mixed with cauterizations, and apply them to those places.
And if it is in the summer, and the sites are fleshy, then you should place cotton soaked in water and oil or wine and oil, and let it be for three days as we have said; then pierce the pustule, cleanse it, and administer whatever suits it according to what has been said until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary to know about the cure of pustules universally, but according to the way of distinction I have said before, so I have spoken particularly about each pustule in its own chapter.
Chapter 41.
Of the section of pustules that come in the membrane of the head.
In the membrane of the head there are small pustules, and they contain nodules which are formed from them; and their species are many.
And from them are blisters, and from those containing moisture similar to lime. And from those there are which contain moisture similar to ash, and also similar to them; and from those there are which are scaly and hard.
And in the section of all of them, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, although you should be careful not to cut the arteries.
And the operation in the section of those is that you express them with an instrument the form of which you will see below, the one which is called a probe, so that you know what it contains.
For if what is contained is moisture, then you should split it with a section according to its length by a superficial section in this form:
And you should begin the section from line .B to line .G; so that when the moisture is evacuated, then you should scrape off that in which the moisture was contained, and not leave any of it behind, for repeatedly returning, if there is any cause remaining.
And then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment, if it is available, or else in water and salt; and fill it with that, and let it sit overnight, for by that you will corrode everything that remains of that membrane.
And then apply ointment to it again secondly and thirdly if it needs it, while you are confident that no cause of that membrane remains; then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed.
And if the pustule contains a nodule of fat, then you should split it according to this form: by making a section having the shape of a cross, and cut the edges between the two lips of the section and scrape it entirely from every part, and use your strength in extracting the membrane which contains that.
But if an artery causes a contradiction to you, then do what I have told you primarily.
And similarly do in the pustule which is lapidified by section and cure as I have said to you; and section on a lapidified pustule is pus-like, for it is of little blood and little moisture.
And sometimes some of these pustules are in the head in some people in whom there is not moisture at all; that cause is that they split one on the head of an old woman and plug up the pustule with a piece of hard, rough, white pebble, which could not be moved, and if anyone hit it, it bled.
But in other pustules which are accidental in the head, this is not that chapter; except for those which come on the heads of children and from the roots of the ears, but the section of all of them should be a superficial section.
And make the incision at the lower end of them, so that the body is relieved from illness to its lower parts.
Then cure these with what you consider appropriate for healing.
Chapter 42.
Of the cutting of scrofula which happens in the neck.
These bumps often appear on the neck, armpits and angles of the joints, and sometimes elsewhere in the body.
And those that happen in the neck are some that are engendered among them and all scrofula of these is within its own envelope, as we have already described, as well as with nodes and bumps on the head.
And there are different kinds of scrofula: some are hard, some contain moisture and some are malignant and resistant to treatment.
Therefore in one where you see a good disposition in the touch, of which the color that is apparent approaches the color of the skin, and it is swollen to all parts, and is not annexed to the nerves of the neck, or to the veins, or to the arteries, and is not deep, you ought to cut into this with a superficial incision from above the body to below the line of 10 between the lines of GI and GB and scrape off all around it, and extend two lips of the skin with pincers or with small forceps if you have need of those, as we have said in the bumps on the head, and extract this little by little.
And it is more important that the vein or nerve not be cut.
And the spatula must not be sharp, so that you do not touch with it or hurt the patient, and you ought to cut only what is necessary to cut, for if you cut a vein or artery and stop your operation, then put on the wound vitriol in powder or other powders that stop blood flow, close the wound, and leave there that which causes the acuity of the bump to cease and the wound to soften and begin to be suppurative. When the blood is abstained.
Therefore return to your operation until you have finished it.
And then inquire with your finger if there is any cause of the other small scrofula, therefore cut into those and clean them.
And if in the root of the large scrofula there is a vein, then you ought not to cut that scrofula from its root. And so that it falls by itself without harm, you ought to press this with a folded cloth and let it drop until it falls down of itself.
Then fill the wound with old wine in which you have already soaked Egyptian ointment and cure this.
And if you cut the scrofula entirely then you ought to press together the two lips of the wound and stop immediately any pus that has not run out.
But if you see that there is pus running out due to the size of the scrofula then you ought to understand cutting into its root and opening it up and administering cauterization and what is said.
And those of the scrofula which contain moisture, pierce this with a superficial incision where you see the site of maturation of it to be, and make an incision so that the pus runs out from the bottom of the body as we have said.
And then administer an incision, apply a cautery and plasters to these that the suppuration is stopped. And then when you see the wound already cleaned, cure this with ointment of generative flesh until it is healed.
Chapter 43.
Of the cutting of the pus of bumps in the gullet.
The ancients wrote about this incision in the pilhot and I have not seen any person in our land who has had it done.
And this is the inscription of their language.
But in men who have a constriction, if the extraction of the pilhot is avoided for fear that all the veins and the major nerves of the patient are there.
But in those who have bumps cauterized in the mouth or gullet or two ears, when the patient is not in the throat, then it is useful to do the incision of the pilhot to avoid the harm that happens by piercing.
Therefore when we want this then let us cut the pilhot below three circles of the circles of the pilhot or four with small incision for the breadth in that which is between two circles for quantity, and the incision should be in pharynx not in the cartilage and that place is convenient to incision because it is deprived of flesh and the vessels of blood are there.
And if the doctor is fearful then let him extend the skin of the gullet with pincers and then split the skin so that it reaches the canal but avoid the vessels of blood if you see any cause for that.
And then cut the larynx according to what we have described, and it is indicated about the incision of the canal by the flame which is of that which has exited from that which is of him broken apart and by the piercing of the voice.
And let the wound remain open for some time.
Therefore when the time is healed in which the piercing is feared, draw together two lips of the skin of the wound and split only that which is the cartilage.
And then administer medicines which make flesh grow so that it may be healed.
And Abucasis said that the sum of their language, the exposure is only that some of these bumps have been cauterized in the gullet of the patient and the patient has come to death and his throat is cut through and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe through the site of the wound by any breathing and he is saved from death.
And for that they commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed and the malice of it is for three days then afterwards he commanded to close the wound and cure this so that it may be healed.
And that which I have seen by my doctors is that it serves for a woman to press one breast and moisten it in the gullet of the patient and cut into there one part of the canal of the lung, and he was called to the cure of him and discovered the wound and found the blood which had run out from the wound.
Therefore he confessed that this had not cut vein nor artery and the wound bled out from it and he cured this so that the fire was healed.
And did not consent to the servant unless she had applied in the voice and then after some days he returned to the examination of his dispositions.
And now I say that in the incision of the pilhot there is no fear.

Of the cutting on bumps which happen in the gullet outward and is called hernia of the gullet.
This hernia of the gullet is a great hernia according to the color of the body and it happens in women.

De le podrague e de los podraguers.
Of the gout and gouty nodes.
There are many types of nodes, and I have already described them all in the division above.
And whoever wishes to know the difference between a node and an ulcer, let him ponder this.
And I say that with an ulcer there is heat and fever and violent pains until the ebullition of the superfluous matter is stopped; and there is a completed putrefaction when the fever, pain and heat cease.
But if there are pains and heat without it being necessary to call it gout then it should be cauterized in order to be cured.
And it is according to the color of the body and the origin of it is like a cyst and it happens in this way with a vacuole, whether it is greater or smaller, and they are according to two species, either fatty or containing humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, as I described in the division.
And whoever, when he comes to the cure of a nodule, cuts it and probes it at the beginning with an instrument called an intromens, according to its form which will come in the chapter which is next.
And it is the way of examining pustules and all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and put it into the moist place which you find in the pustule, and turn your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the membrane.
And then close your hand according to the size of the pustule and take out the instrument and consider what has come out through its orifice.
And if the humidity has drained away of whatever color it is then you cut into it superficially as I have said in other pustules.
And if there is no humidity coming out through the orifice of the instrument then you know it is fatty.
And dry over it by cutting into it in the form of a cross according to this form: And you cut into it as I have taught you and suspend it by pins and excise the membrane from all sides with ease and keep the skin or sac over it and draw out that pus with the nodule.
But if it is broken in the operation and it is not possible to draw out that pus then you take it away by pieces so that nothing remains within it that could cause its rupture again.
For if something remains within it then the nodule will return according to the more or less.
And if you see that a small part remains within it then complete the poultice with some sharp and corrosive powders and strengthen the poultice and put it over where the pustule is cauterized and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large nodule then you split its two lips and cure it with that which it incarnates.
But if there is no pulse or a weak pulse then you cut and fill the place with ground vitriol which is powdered and let it rest for two days or three until the poultice hardens, and then return to cutting what has broken of the nodule.

Of the cure of the breasts of men which are resembling those of women.

Of the puncturing of apoplexy that comes from below, the twitching.

Chapter 49.
On the cutting of abscesses that happen through an artery or a vein.
And the signs by which you can tell that inflammation and abscess are caused by an artery or vein: and when an abscess is caused by an artery it occurs deep inside the body; and when you press on the abscess, if you feel a pulse in it, this indicates a stridor.
And that which is caused by a vein is round at the surface of the body.
And cutting into this abscess is dangerous, especially in those that are beneath the armpits, and in the angles, and on the neck, and in many other parts of the body; and it is very great, so it should be avoided.
But if they are caused by inflammation of the opening of an artery, cut into the artery in the long axis; and once you have opened the artery with pincers, and have uncovered the tunics inside,
And then put an awl into it and force it to penetrate to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places — which will cause you to tie it off in extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then plug up the place between the two ligaments with sputum so that all the blood in it is dried up and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer treatment so that pus is produced inside it until the ligaments fall away, and then cure that with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess caused by cutting of a vein, then you must hold what is above the abscess with your hand as firmly as you can, and then thrust in the awl underneath that place which you are holding with your hand, and force it to penetrate; and let there be a double thread in it so that you extract it from the other side, and then tie off the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you before about the ligament of the grape in two parts with two ends of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then put in the awl underneath the whole abscess behind the first incision of the awl and constrict your double threads in four places.
Then dry up the abscess in its middle place so that when it has drained out what is inside it, you insert your instrument into the superfluity of the artery and leave behind what is tied to it.
And then place on it a powder which you have submerged in wine and oil, and then administer the treatment which is made with leeches and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 50: Of the abscess which happens from the twisting of nerves.
Just as abscesses can happen in arteries and veins, so also can they happen in nerves when they happen from a blow or happen because of some other similar thing.
And it is most often done in the places of the auxiliaries or of the talus, or in any place where there are joints in the body.
And it is a grave abscess and is the same colour as the rest of the body, and there are many veins in it, and when it is constricted with violence, the patient feels a stupor throughout his body.
And it is not an abscess located in the cavity of the body, and therefore it is beneath the artery, and it is beaten at all parts and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
So it is not necessary for those which are in the joints to be cauterized with iron, because they will quickly develop a contraction.
But that which is on the head or forehead, open the artery with sputum. But if it is a small abscess, then cut it out with forceps and cut off its roots.
But if it is large, then suspend it with a hook and cut it out, and then put a patch over it; and stitch together the wound, and cure that until it is healed.
Chapter 51.
On the cutting of an abscess which happens in the jaw which happens in the belly.
Many people experience in their bellies and in other parts of their bodies a certain kind of abscesses which are called by a likeness to mushrooms because their roots are thin but the top is large; and they have twisted lips, and they are either small or very large.
And I myself have seen one, and in his belly were two which were like mushroom-like, and there was no difference between them white, of very thin roots.
And the lips of these were turned inside out and torn, and moisture ran from it all the time.
So I cut into them and found in one of them stones weighing 15 ounces. And the other 6 ounces.
And the operation at the incision of these is that you should consider whether the patient is moist, and if the colour of the wound is white, moist, of thin roots, then you cut into it with sputum lengthwise, and they will be cauterized in the fire, because many times blood is expelled from the incision; and if you see blood, cauterize that.
And if the patient is timid and fearful, be careful not to cut into him with iron; but take some new lead wire and constrict that wound, in the manner which we have said before; and leave it for two days.
And then tighten the lead wire in the constriction; so do not cease to constrict it with the large lead, until it is cut off and falls away by itself.
But if the wound is of thick roots, then in its incision there is some cause for fear and horror, especially in that which is in the belly.
But it is possible that you cut out the matrix of it, and then cauterize that so that it does not return.
And then cure that until the wound is healed.
And be careful not to assume that you will cut out a wound which is of dusky colour, of little feeling, of regular guard, because that is an abscess.
And I came by memory to the skull.
Chapter 52.
On the treatment of an abscess in the navel.
Abscess in the navel is caused by many causes; or by fissures of the diaphragm which is above the belly, and from it the membrane or bowels slip inside according to other ruptures; or by blood which flows from a vein or artery as has been said before, or by constriction of the intestines.
But if it is from a fissure of the diaphragm and a slip of the membrane, then the colour of the abscess is like that of the body; and there is little pain in it, and it appears in various places. And if it is from a rupture of the bowels, then its location according to what we have said before, with more violent diversity, and when you press that with your fingers, it is concealed, and then returns; and it is very large inside, and is magnified by the taking in of food and violent labour.
But if it is from moisture, then it is easy to feel and is not concealed when you press with your hand, nor constricted, nor cut.
And if it is due to blood, then with these signs the abscess will decline towards blackness.
But if it is due to flesh, then the abscess is heavy, large and hard, and it is located according to a certain amount.
But if it is due to windiness, then its touch is leonine.
And the operation on it is that you consider whether the prominence of the navel is due to arterial blood, or venous blood, or windiness; then you must abstain from the cure of it, for in that there is fear and dread as I instructed in the chapter where I discussed abscesses from arteries and veins.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to the intestine or hernia, then you must command the patient to hold his breath and be standing extended; and then sign with your hand around the entire navel, and then command him to breathe in towards your palm on his chest, and then circle with your finger around the navel over the area which you have marked with your hand; and then extend the majority of the abscess upwards with a large needle; and then bind around the area with strong thread or twine, and the manner of binding decent.
And then open the middle of the extended abscess over the ligament and insert your finger into that opening and seek out the intestine; and if you have caught it or retained it by the ligament, then you extract it and push the intestine back inside the belly.
And if you have caught the hernia, then take that with a needle; and incise the excess of it.
But if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then surround that mark, and then return to your operation; and take two needles and put on them strong threads, and insert the two needles into the circuit which you have made around the abscess in a crosswise manner, so that they may penetrate; and then tighten the abscess in four places over the needles.
And if you want, remove the needles and allow the extended flesh to fall back in and heal by itself; or incise what is sottile and will heal, and then cure that with water which is good for wounds.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to flesh in it or humidity, then you must hollow out the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or humidity which you find in it, and then cure that with water which covers it and consolidates the area.
Chapter 53:
On the cure of a hernia.
We have already said, in the division, about the kind of hernia and in what way there is a path to its cure by medicines, and that it is different in it the cure by iron so that it not be ulcerated; and we have said about hernias engendered in the mother and caution in the cure of them.
And the ancients said that in some cases hernias are in a place where their eradication is possible, as with those in the breasts or the groin and their similar parts assigned to be extracted from, especially when they begin small.
But when it is old and large, you must not approach it, for I have not seen that any such one has healed from it nor that one has come to that.
And the operation on it when it is allocated as we have said, is that you precede and let the patient and purge from black bile in some cases, and then bleed that one if a manifest fullness is found.
And then prepare the patient with preparation in which he will be located for operation, and then prohibit in the wound hooked tools which go there; and then hollow out all parts with good cutting until no cause of the hernia remains. And let the blood flow, and do not cut that loosely, and squeeze out the places, and wipe away all the clotted blood with your hand or with an instrument by which it is possible for you from among instruments.
But if it causes contrary from clotted blood flowing from a vein or artery, then cauterize that one until the flow of blood is ceased, and then cure that with the other cure until it is healed.
Chapter 54:
On the cure of hydropsy.
We have already recommended, in the division, about the kinds of hydropsy from water, and the signs of each kind, about the cure of it by medicines.
And that one which is cured by iron is only the kind of solitus, and it is not approached by iron to the kind of tympany or to the kind of hiposarca, for that one is deadly.
And when you have treated this kind of hydropsy tympany with medicines and it does not respond to your medicine, then consider, for if the patient already has acquired debility, or is with another malady, another hydropsy, as if it is in him coughing or an ache in the belly and similar to those, then guard yourself that you do not treat him with iron, for fear is over that.
But if you see the patient of healthy exuberance, and with him there is not another malady but hydropsy only, and not a child or old person, then the manner of the operation on him is that you elevate the patient between your palms, and then he will press his belly with his palm, pushing the water to the part below the navel, and then take spatha spiny according to this form:
It should have two acute parts long, with an acute extremity as spatha; but nevertheless it must be in him some shortness little by little, so that in the operation with it you do not pass into the intestine, and lead that one.
And then consider if the generation of hydropsy is from parts of the intestines, for then you must with the section lengthen the navel to the amount of three fingers to the parts below, in the right of him over the navel.
But if the generation of hydropsy is from malady of the liver, then your section must be left of the navel by three fingers.
And if the generation of it is from the spleen, then your section must be in the right.
And do not let your section be over the side over which the patient wants to lie so that the excesses do not flow to that place.

But if the hernia occurs in all the vessels, then either extract the testicles or that the testicles are privated from their food by the incision of the vessels so that there is no benefit to them, or that they are withered because of it.
Chapter .lxv.
Of the cure of intestinal hernia.
The occurrence of this hernia is from an incision that extends into the head over the belly from the parts of the angles of the navel of the belly so that the intestines are pushed out through that rupture in some intestines.
And this rupture is either of the head or from an incision there, and both species occur for many causes: either from a blow, or from saucing, or from crying, or from the elevation of some heavy cause, or from the like.
And the sign of this, when it is from an extension of the head, is that it occurs little by little over a long time and does not occur suddenly, and it is a hard pustule between the veil and the skin because the head compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it is when it is from an incision in the head, for at the beginning it causes violent pain suddenly; and there are divers appearances beneath the skin near the genitals, and that is from thrusting out of the intestine, and the body of it appears at the parts below the navel of the belly.
And sometimes the membrane is thrust out with the intestine, and this hernia is called intestinal hernia of the bowels.
And sometimes it is caused by windiness, and sometimes there is a fissure in the intestine, and here it is retained, and it is very harmful for the patient, and sometimes it causes bad pain and most when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of these species of this disease with iron there is fear, for it is necessary to avoid the cautery in that.
And the manner of the operation for this is to command the patient to reduce the intestine with his hand at its parts inside its cavity if he obeys its returnment, and then have him bent over so that his chest is between your hands, and lift his legs.
And then tighten the one which covers the genitals at its parts above, and insert the needle of the genitals all through its length; and then fix in two lips of the incision hooks according to how you open it with those.
And if the incision according to the amount that for you is possible, then from that the head is pushed out.
And then scrape those chaps which are beneath the genitals, so that the white head of the head is uncovered in all its parts.
Then you insert your finger in that which covers the testicle, where there is between the white head and the head according to the second one, and release with that the adhesion which is behind the head.
And then hold with your hand the one which covers the genitals at its parts outside, and extend the white head in him with your left hand, and lift up the head with the head at the place of the incision; and command the servant to extend the intestine within you and you dissolve that adhesion behind with completed solucio.
And approach with your fingers so that there is no cause of the intestine being wrapped in the white head. But if you press on it for any cause, then you insert that into the belly below.
And then incise in the part below the scrotum by section, of which blood and pus will flow out just as we have commanded in what we have said.
And then administer wool submerged in oil and place it on the wound; and administer the bandage which we have commanded (and some times the scrotum is cauterized, which we have said near the incision of it they fear from a flow of blood, for many times this happens) and let the bandage fall within so that by itself it may drop.
But if the healing of it is delayed, then let there be applied warm water, and place it over that within which falls according to what we have said.
And then heal the wound with the other healing of wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 66:
Of the hernial hernia.
In this hernia I have not seen anyone who has been burned on the cure of it with iron.

Chapter 67:
Of the disruption which is made in the angles.
Sometimes there is a rupture in the angles as we have said and the place protrudes.
And the genitalia should not be any cause of the intestines to the genitalia; and if they are, that is few; and return to it in all hours.
But if the time of that is prolonged, a fissure is made in the scrotum from which the intestine descends into the scrotum; and this happens by the extension of the scrotum which is in the angles as we have said, the cause being that the scrotum is stretched, and then it softens and the place is abscessed and protrudes.
And the cure of it is with cauterization thus as is preceded by the narration of it.
And sometimes it is cured with iron thus: and the patient hangs over his head between your hands, and then dries up the place of the rupture of the abscesses protrude by section to the breadth according to the quantity of three fingers.
And then strengthen the white scrotum which is below the scrotum so that it is uncovered.

And cauterization is better in this place because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68:
Of the softening of the scrotum of the testicles.
Many times the scrotum of the testicles in some men is softened because the flesh that is between it is softened and the guarding of it is lost.
Therefore it is necessary that he who is practiced in the cure of it makes the patient lie according to his head and incise all the scrotum which is softened over the natural scrotum, and then sew two lips together.
And if you wish, cut off in the beginning the superfluity of the softened scrotum with three or four cuts and with firm suturing.
And then incise between the sutures, and then heal by the healing of the other wounds until it is healed and the testicles fall down.
Chapter 69:
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but for the cause it is read to me that I remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except by two ways, of which one is that it be in the science of the doctor when he is questioned about it, so that he knows the cure of it from which happens; and the other way is that we many times have had the necessity of castration of other beasts for our young ones because of them, just as of horses, and of oxen, and of pigs, and of beasts similar to the beasts.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: or by tearing, or by incision to section.
But in that which is done by tearing, the way of the operation is that we cause the beast to lie in warm water so that its testicles are softened and hang down and that they are cut off. And then take them with your hand so that they are resolved and do not appear underneath the touch.
But in castration done by incision and section, see that you have the beast and press the scrotum of its testicles with your left hand.
And then ligate the suspensory ligament, and incise over each eye with one section so that two eyes are processed.
And then incise those which you will have bled. And do not cause over those of the scrotum any cause except the subtle scrotum which is over the veins.
And this way of castration is better which is done by tearing because tearing leaves no cause of the testicles so that the beast desires coitus.
And then heal the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70:
Of the cure of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men is according to two ways: one is when or appears the space between the scrotum of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles figure that clitoris of woman in which there are hairs.
And sometimes from it urine the one which is in the scrotum of the testicles.
But in women it is one species: and it is that the clitoris of woman over the penis is like two testicles of man a little bit of all and foreskin of man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three species: of two of men and of one species of women. And it is that see that you incise those tightened flesh so that the impression of it flow out, and then heal those with the healing of the other wounds.
And in the second species of men of which it flows urine which is in the scrotum of the testicles there is no cure or operation in it.

And then you who have the superfluity of linen with your hand or with a cloth and insert it.

Chapter 72:
On the cure of an inguinal hernia.
A hernia is when the vagina of a woman is not perforated or the hole is small. It can be natural or accidental.
An accidental hernia is caused by gout which preceded it, and it is made either by a membrane that is too tight or by a thin or hard cyst.
And it happens either in the opening of the mother's womb, or in her ribs, or in the upper part of her belly, or in the lower part, and it prohibits coitus and pregnancy, and strongly prohibits menstruation.
And the knowledge of it is gained by observation of the midwife, if the pregnancy is apparent, it is a premature delivery; but if not apparent, then you examine it with your fingers or with your hand.
But if the pregnancy is by a thin cyst and it is close to both labia, then you cut and rupture it.
And you place on both labia some powder, and you place your fingers indicating in both hands.
And the woman should be on her back, with her thighs stretched out, and you stretch both labia with force so that the thin cyst is broken and the pregnancy is opened.
And then take wool and dip it in oil and place it on the wound, and let him go for a walk during the day so that the cut is not healed closed.
But if the cyst is large and thick, then you should cut it with a spatule or with a blade of myrrh.
But if the pregnancy is by membrane, then suspend it with oil and cut it.
And you should have the medicines that stop bleeding without biting, such as aconite, dragon's blood, and gum arabic, adjusted with egg white of an eagle owl.
And then administer a wide lead cane so that the wound is not closed too quickly.
And hold it for several days and administer cold water.
And then it should be cured with the other cure of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes accidents happen in the mother's birth of other meats, and then you should cut according to this manner. But if it is by a crust, then there should be no contradiction to the crust with iron in any way.
Chapter 73:
On the cure of hemorrhoids, and of tail, and of red botch that happens in the vagina of women.
Hemorrhoids are an appearance of openings of many veins from which flow much blood continuously; and when they are old hemorrhoids and are swollen.
And I have already said in the division of these their kinds and their signs, and say thus those that receive cure and those that do not receive cure.
Therefore I say that hemorrhoids and theyls when they are in the opening of the mother's womb and do not appear in sensation, then in those there should be no cure with iron.
But those which are in the opening of the mother's womb over which there is sensation, these are the ones that are cured.
And you should put the woman in a bath and stretch them with tweezers or with rough cloth, and cut them with blades.
And then sprinkle over them the flow of blood of one of the powdery medicines without biting, thus with aconite and similar to these.
And then let her walk for an hour, and then place her in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then do it again with a poultice made of sumac and husks of pomegranates and walnut shells and similar.
And then take flour of wheat and cook it in a bath with honey and sour wine and make a poultice with this over its back.
And if the blood is dried up, it is good; and if not, do the sticking with two leeches, and to the nipples its escarification.
And then take wool and soak it in juice of colander or in juice of wild basil or in juice of wild garlic with red wine and place it on the wound; and then cure the wound with ointments until it is healed.
And cure it until it is healed.
Chapter 74:
On the accidental piercing of the eardrum in the mother's womb.

Chapter 75:
To instruct midwives on how to treat stillborn children, when their shape is not natural.
It is necessary that the midwife recognize in the beginning the shape of a natural childbirth by its signs, and it is when you see the woman expressing her breasts, and desiring to breathe the air, and feeling relaxed over what is above her, and hastening the birth of the child, then you know that this position is according to a natural shape, and it is the delivery of it over their head, and the second one with it suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord.
Therefore, when you see those signs, then the belly should be compressed so that the embryo descends gently, and when it is over their head, they deliver the second one, and the placenta is removed with a good cleansing.
But when this childbirth is not natural and laudable, because the child is born on its feet, and their body comes out before their head and their feet, or when one of their hands or feet is born first, or when their head and hand are born, or when the belly is delivered first, and very soon it is returned to their neck, and resembling one of these non-laudable shapes.
It is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and guard against error and deception.
And I will show you all the figures of them, and what cunning is in them so that it may be understood by this and be established upon it.
When the child is born over their head through natural exertion, and it is violent on the woman and a difficult delivery for them, and you see the strength of her already weakened, then make that incision, or if the women are holding onto it, evaporate their grip with fenugreek powder and with oiled rags.
And the midwife should insert her finger between their teeth gently and push with it the second one, or dry it up with her fingernail in between so that she removes what is inside it of moisture. And press the woman's belly so that the child goes down.
But if it does not come out, then the woman should be anointed with a mixture of styrax and fenugreek with honey.
And the midwife, who is anointing it, should compress and make that sneeze with seasoning; and hold their mouth and nose for an hour, because the child will be forced out immediately.
And if both of the child' hands are born first at the beginning, then you should draw them back little by little gently. But if she does not obey the instrument, then place the woman on a plank and raise their feet up, and the plank should be tilted towards the ground; and the woman should be held so that she does not fall from the tilt.
And if the hands are not turned inside out and the child is stillborn, then insert those and pull the child's arm or tie the body to their hand with a cloth and pull it equally, because that will be forced out.
When the child is born on their feet, then you should push those up, and the child will turn little by little, and when you have taken one of their feet, extend those little by little.
But when it is born between their thighs, then you command them to push out, and make that sneeze with seasoning, because it will be forced out if God wills it.
And if it is not forced out with what we have recommended, then return the child little by little to where they should be according to the natural shape, because it will be forced out later with easier delivery.
And if it is prohibited by all that we have recommended, then take of a mixture of aloe and dissolved gum, and beat them both in the mortar with good beating, and line with that the inside of the woman' vagina, the lowest part of the belly. And then make her sweat in lukewarm water, so that she gets rid of phlegm.
And when you see that the breasts are softened, then make fumigation of myrrh and apply to it what is below. And when you have made fumigation for an hour, then make her sneeze on a plank, and then make that sneeze and open the mouth of it, and lift up from there, and press the lowest part of the belly gently, because the child will be forced out immediately.
Delivery of the child hanging from one of their hands. It should be understood as reduction of the hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her bend.
And if she cannot bend, then make her lie on the bed, and press their thighs with violent pressing, and administer to them what they have been prescribed of mucilages.
And if the delivery has come, then make her sneeze on the plank, and then study on reduction of the hand, and turn the child according to the natural shape, and make the woman sneeze and command them to push so that it is forced out.
Delivery of the child on their neck with their arms and belly expanded towards their mother's back. It should be that the midwife holds the hand of the child and then turns it little by little, and it will be with ease.
And when it is out and the umbilical cord is cut, then apply to it what we have recommended of oil and mucilages.
And then command the mother to suckle it little by little, and when she has done that, then make her sneeze on a plank and command them to be tilted to the right side, and then command them to compress it; and make that sneeze with seasoning. The preparation of the fetus is placed on its side.
When you see that the mother is giving birth according to this manner, consider and then insert your finger inside so that the humidity is evacuated.
And if the child is suspended above its face and neck, then insert that of the umbilical cord, so that it is not retained and dies.
Then pull the child to its limbs inside so that you pause that according to what covers it, and command the woman to compress herself in several places, and let it be extracted easily if God wills it.
The exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born in many places, and sometimes three or four, but this is strange and rare; but there are several causes of nature, and not life.
And count those, that they may be multiplied, a second one, and are separated by the umbilical cord, distinguish those within the ligament in the umbilical of each of them. And sometimes they are extracted like a single fetus with a natural easy delivery, and sometimes some are delivered with an un-laudable delivery as we have mentioned above.
And if they are difficult to deliver and reach that which we have said about the unnatural shapes, then you cure those as we have related.
And if the midwife acts sutilly and does that which she does with facilitaion and subtlety, and delay, and is ingenious according to every shape according to how it is prepared in her womb leading to health.
The remembrance of that which forms in the matrix from embryos and abortions.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and up to ten, and I have indeed seen a woman miscarry six times, while another had ten, all formed, due to the wise men measuring them out.
And all that is hidden from that which is in the science of the midwife how powerful she goes to that small one resembling it and therefore pause over there.
Chapter .lxxvi.
